<li id="cite_note-res-181"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-res_181-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation" id="CITEREFFinch1984">Finch, Peter (1984), <i>Ludwig Wittgenstein, Culture and Value</i>, Chicago: University of Chicago Press, p. 33, <q>What inclines even me to believe in Christ's resurrection? I play as it were with the thought.–If he did not rise from the dead, then he decomposed in the grave like every human being. He is dead &amp; decomposed. In that case he is a teacher, like any other &amp; can no longer help; &amp; we are once more orphaned &amp; alone. And have to make do with wisdom &amp; speculation. It is as though we are in a hell, where we can only dream &amp; are shut out from heaven, roofed in as it were. But if I am to be REALLY redeemed,– I need certainty–not wisdom, dreams, speculation–and this certainty is faith. And faith is faith in what my heart, my soul, needs, not my speculative intellect. For my soul, with its passions, as it were with its flesh and blood, must be redeemed, not my abstract mind. Perhaps one may say: Only love can believe the Resurrection. Or: it is love that believes the Resurrection</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALudwig+Wittgenstein&amp;rft.aufirst=Peter&amp;rft.aulast=Finch&amp;rft.btitle=Ludwig+Wittgenstein%2C+Culture+and+Value&amp;rft.date=1984&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.pages=33&amp;rft.place=Chicago&amp;rft.pub=University+of+Chicago+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-182"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-182">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Norman Malcolm; G. H. Von Wright (2001). <i>Ludwig Wittgenstein: A Memoir</i>. <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University_Press" title="Oxford University Press">Oxford University Press</a>. pp. 59–60. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780199247592" title="Special:BookSources/9780199247592">9780199247592</a>. <q>I believe that Wittgenstein was prepared by his own character and experience to comprehend the idea of a judging and redeeming God. But any cosmological conception of a Deity, derived from the notions of cause or of infinity, would be repugnant to him. He was impatient with 'proofs' of the existence of God, and with attempts to give religion a rational foundation. ...I do not wish to give the impression that Wittgenstein accepted any religious faith—he certainly did not—or that he was a religious person. But I think that there was in him, in some sense, the possibility of religion. I believe that he looked on religion as a 'form of life' (to use an expression from the Investigations) in which he did not participate, but with which he was sympathetic and which greatly interested him. Those who did participate he respected — although here as elsewhere he had contempt for insincerity. I suspect that he regarded religious belief as based on qualities of character and will that he himself did not possess. Of Smythies and Anscombe, both of whom had become Roman Catholics, he once said to me: 'I could not possibly bring myself to believe all the things that they believe.' I think that in this remark he was not disparaging their belief. It was rather an observation about his own capacity.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALudwig+Wittgenstein&amp;rft.btitle=Ludwig+Wittgenstein%3A+A+Memoir&amp;rft.date=2001&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=9780199247592&amp;rft.pages=59-60&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span> <span class="citation-comment" style="display:none; color:#33aa33">CS1 maint: Uses authors parameter (<a href="/wiki/Category:CS1_maint:_Uses_authors_parameter" title="Category:CS1 maint: Uses authors parameter">link</a>)</span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-183"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-183">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Tim Labron (2006). <i>Wittgenstein's Religious Point of View</i>. <a href="/wiki/Continuum_International_Publishing_Group" title="Continuum International Publishing Group">Continuum International Publishing Group</a>. p. 47. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780826490278" title="Special:BookSources/9780826490278">9780826490278</a>. <q>Wittgenstein has no goal to either support or reject religion; his only interest is to keep discussions, whether religious or not, clear.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALudwig+Wittgenstein&amp;rft.au=Tim+Labron&amp;rft.btitle=Wittgenstein%27s+Religious+Point+of+View&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=9780826490278&amp;rft.pages=47&amp;rft.pub=Continuum+International+Publishing+Group&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-184"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-184">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">William Child (2011). <i>Wittgenstein</i>. Taylor &amp; Francis. p. 218. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781136731372" title="Special:BookSources/9781136731372">9781136731372</a>. <q>"Was Wittgenstein religious? If we call him an agnostic, this must not be understood in the sense of the familiar polemical agnosticism that concentrates, and prides itself, on the argument that man could never know about these matters. The idea of a God in the sense of the Bible, the image of God as the creator of the world, hardly ever engaged Wittgenstein's attention..., but the notion of a last judgement was of profound concern to him." - (Engelmann)</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALudwig+Wittgenstein&amp;rft.au=William+Child&amp;rft.btitle=Wittgenstein&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=9781136731372&amp;rft.pages=218&amp;rft.pub=Taylor+%26+Francis&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-185"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-185">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Edward Kanterian (2007). <i>Ludwig Wittgenstein</i>. <a href="/wiki/Reaktion_Books" title="Reaktion Books">Reaktion Books</a>. pp. 145–146. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781861893208" title="Special:BookSources/9781861893208">9781861893208</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALudwig+Wittgenstein&amp;rft.au=Edward+Kanterian&amp;rft.btitle=Ludwig+Wittgenstein&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=9781861893208&amp;rft.pages=145-146&amp;rft.pub=Reaktion+Books&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/E._L._Doctorow" title="E. L. Doctorow">Doctorow, E. L.</a> <i>City of God</i>. Plume, 2001, depicts an imaginary rivalry between Wittgenstein and Einstein.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Apostolos_Doxiadis" title="Apostolos Doxiadis">Doxiadis, Apostolos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christos_Papadimitriou" title="Christos Papadimitriou">Papadimitriou, Christos</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Logicomix" title="Logicomix">Logicomix</a></i>. Bloomsbury, 2009.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bruce_Duffy" title="Bruce Duffy">Duffy, Bruce</a>. <i>The World as I Found It</i>. Ticknor &amp; Fields, 1987, a recreation of Wittgenstein's life.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Derek_Jarman" title="Derek Jarman">Jarman, Derek</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Wittgenstein_(film)" title="Wittgenstein (film)">Wittgenstein</a></i>, a biopic of Wittgenstein with a script by <a href="/wiki/Terry_Eagleton" title="Terry Eagleton">Terry Eagleton</a>, British Film Institute, 1993.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Philip_Kerr" title="Philip Kerr">Kerr, Philip</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/A_Philosophical_Investigation" title="A Philosophical Investigation">A Philosophical Investigation</a></i>, Chatto &amp; Windus, 1992, a dystopian thriller set in 2012.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/David_Markson" title="David Markson">Markson, David</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Wittgenstein%27s_Mistress" title="Wittgenstein's Mistress">Wittgenstein's Mistress</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Dalkey_Archive_Press" title="Dalkey Archive Press">Dalkey Archive Press</a>, 1988, an experimental novel, a first-person account of what it would be like to live in the world of the <i>Tractatus</i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/James_Tully_(philosopher)" title="James Tully (philosopher)">Tully, James</a>. <i>Strange Multiplicity: Constitutionalism in an Age of Diversity</i>. Cambridge: Cambridge University Press, 1995</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/David_Foster_Wallace" title="David Foster Wallace">Wallace, David Foster</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Broom_of_the_System" title="The Broom of the System">The Broom of the System</a></i>. Penguin Books, 1987, a novel.</li>
</ul>
